<div id="review_3143717237" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3143717237" />
    <a title="La La" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17265997-la-la"><img alt="La La" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468213406p2/17265997.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3143717237?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="La La" class="user" itemprop="url" name="La La" href="/user/show/17265997-la-la">La La</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17265997-la-la?shelf=read-classics">read-classics</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17265997-la-la?shelf=want-physical-shelf">want-physical-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3143717237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2635938600599143158">I still loved this book! I think this is the third time I have read it. The author is skilled at painting visuals. He has a way of describing women's bodies in detail without sexualizing them. He can be describing breasts and it is the same as if he were describing a man's beard. I appreciated this because in the story it subtly showed how a woman's appearance in the '50s had a lot to do with how she was viewed as a person, and how it affected the way others' interacted with them.<br/><br/>The story was m</span>
  <span id="freeText2635938600599143158" style="display:none">I still loved this book! I think this is the third time I have read it. The author is skilled at painting visuals. He has a way of describing women's bodies in detail without sexualizing them. He can be describing breasts and it is the same as if he were describing a man's beard. I appreciated this because in the story it subtly showed how a woman's appearance in the '50s had a lot to do with how she was viewed as a person, and how it affected the way others' interacted with them.<br /><br />The story was more than semi-autobiographical. I think it is only considered Fiction because names and places had been changed. It's a fantastic reflection of how Black people are judged on a different level than White people; in the 1950s if you were uneducated and White you were still viewed as superior to an educated Black man. He got used to being respected and accepted when he was wearing his military uniform during his service days, but once discharged into the civilian world things changed.<br /><br />I also love stories about passionate and compassionate teachers who win over tough students. There is so much to love about this book. I was excited to learn there is a sequel, Paid Servant. I'm reading it right now.<br /><br />This was part of my February Black History Month reading during my 2020 A Year of Reading Classics challenge.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2635938600599143158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1984817361" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1984817361" />
    <a title="Celia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30261451-celia"><img alt="Celia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466854747p2/30261451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1984817361?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celia" href="/user/show/30261451-celia">Celia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30261451-celia?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30261451-celia?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30261451-celia?shelf=2016-died">2016-died</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1984817361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13185841077558603407">One of my reading goals this year is to read at least 1 book written by significant authors who died in 2016. This is the sixth book I have read this year.<br/><br/>Once again, I have found an author of significant worth, but unknown to me.<br/><br/>Most who read this will be familiar with the movie of same name starring Sidney Poitier as Mark Thackery. Thackery is actually the pseudonym for Braithwaite. This is, in fact, an autobiography.<br/><br/>Very well written in what I have come to recognize as the British style, it i</span>
  <span id="freeText13185841077558603407" style="display:none">One of my reading goals this year is to read at least 1 book written by significant authors who died in 2016. This is the sixth book I have read this year.<br /><br />Once again, I have found an author of significant worth, but unknown to me.<br /><br />Most who read this will be familiar with the movie of same name starring Sidney Poitier as Mark Thackery. Thackery is actually the pseudonym for Braithwaite. This is, in fact, an autobiography.<br /><br />Very well written in what I have come to recognize as the British style, it is an entertaining and sympathetic treatise.<br /><br />Any teacher will appreciate the successes realized by Braithwaite's unique teaching style. <br /><br />These kids were brought up in a rough part of Soho and their initial reaction to their Negro teacher (this was written in 1959 so Braithwaite does call himself a Negro) mirrors their rough environment.<br /><br />But by the end of the term, due to Braithwaite's approach that treats them as adults, they are polite, charming and grateful.<br /><br />Their last presentment to him, in a nicely wrapped parcel, is embossed To Sir, With Love. I can just hear Lulu singing it now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13185841077558603407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gtPm9O56dk2sphe6S//SDqF1Y+eWhbhI/hY7CcGctszgbJliIbvLt/eG63YjaxFIS72SxOCLdKObqhdvmssb0A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5uQBUpmlr4gNds4kwO6DAVNDPnMU2HXTSyP8cql3br2EW37EVmQSclZWMuioekBHuYvPUGLWuTgun9AU8iDDoQ==')})
  }

It beautifully details the dramatic events of a harrowing winter with months of never-ending blizzards leading to railroad blockades that all but cut off fledgling communities.  But what really happened during the Hard Winter of 1880–81?  Lively and rewarding, The Beautiful Snow is a new look at the Hard Winter. Pulling from nearly three thousand regional newspaper articles, The Beautiful Snow weaves the historical record around and through Wilder’s fictionalized account of The Long Winter. From the tireless efforts to dig out the railroad blockades, to lavish oyster parties, to carefully spun boosterism, the Hard Winter comes to life with extraordinary tales of survival, resilience, and But when he accepted a post in Cuba in the early 1990s, she resolved to keep a detailed diary of her time there, recording her daily experiences as a wife, mother, and foreigner in a land of contraband. The result is a striking, rare glimpse into a tiny country of enormous splendor and squalor. Though the Tattlins are provided with a well-staffed Havana mansion, the store shelves are bare. On the streets, beggars plead for soap, not coins. A vet with few real medical supplies operates on a carved mahogany coffee table in a Louis XIV–style drawing room. The people adore festivity, but Christmas trees are banned. And when Isadora hosts a dinner party whose guest list includes Fidel Castro himself, she observes the ultimate contradiction at the very heart of Cuba. Vividly capturing Cuba’s simultaneously appalling and enchanting essence, Cuba Diaries casts an irresistible spell and lifts the enigma of an island that is trapped in time, but not in       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/39481.E_R_Braithwaite">About E.R. Braithwaite</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/39481.E_R_Braithwaite"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1286209991p3/39481.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/39481.E_R_Braithwaite">E.R. Braithwaite
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
75
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4758682590537281080">E.R. (Edward Ricardo) Braithwaite was a novelist, writer, teacher, and diplomat, best known for his stories of social conditions and racial discrimination against black people. <br/><br/>An alumnus of Queens College, Braithwaite excelled at City University of New York, after which he served in the RAF during WWII as a fighter pilot (1941-45) and then went on to receive an advanced degree in Physics from Cam</span>
  <span id="freeText4758682590537281080" style="display:none">E.R. (Edward Ricardo) Braithwaite was a novelist, writer, teacher, and diplomat, best known for his stories of social conditions and racial discrimination against black people. <br /><br />An alumnus of Queens College, Braithwaite excelled at City University of New York, after which he served in the RAF during WWII as a fighter pilot (1941-45) and then went on to receive an advanced degree in Physics from Cambridge University (1949). Braithwaite also attended the University of London. <br /><br />Unable to establish a career in physics, his chosen field, which he attributed to his status as an ethnic minority, Braithwaite turned to teaching. <br /><br />Braithwaite was perhaps best known as an author for his autobiographical novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/895163.To_Sir_With_Love" title="To Sir With Love" rel="nofollow noopener">To Sir With Love</a> set in an east London secondary school, later directed, produced and adapted for the screen by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6417.james_clavell" title="james clavell" rel="nofollow noopener">james clavell</a> starring Sidney Poitier as a schoolteacher from British Guiana. <br /><br />Braithwaite gave up teaching and continued writing, during this time he became a social worker with the London County Council working to provide foster care for black children. <br /><br />He would later describe these challenging experiences in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/655758.Paid_Servant" title="Paid Servant" rel="nofollow noopener">Paid Servant</a>. <br /><br />Braithwaite's long and exemplary career took him to UNESCO in Paris as an educational consultant and lecturer (1963-1966). Then he served as a Guyanese ambassador in the late sixties. First as Guyanese Ambassador to the United Nations (1967-68), then as Guyanese Ambassador to Venezuela (1968-69). He was World Veterans' Foundation Human Rights Officer, Paris (1960-63).<br /><br />Braithwaite returned to teaching as a professor of English, at New York University and later in 2002 held the position of Writer in Residence at Howard University in Washington DC. <br /><br />Braithwaite was a visiting professor at Manchester Community College, Connecticut, during the 2005-2006 school year, also serving as commencement speaker and receiving an honorary degree.<br /><br />In August 2007 Braithwaite received the Guyana Cultural Association of New York's Exemplary Award for his work as an educator, a diplomat and an author. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4758682590537281080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2147453-to-sir-with-love">Quotes from To Sir, With Love</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
